p.alloc\\n64: }\\n65: \\n66: func (p *page) full() bool {\\n67: \\treturn pageSize-p.alloc < recordHeaderSize\\n68: }\\n69: \\n70: func (p *page) reset() {\\n71: \\tfor i := range p.buf {\\n72: \\t\\tp.buf[i] = 0\\n73: \\t}\\n74: \\tp.alloc = 0\\n75: \\tp.flushed = 0\\n76: }\\n77: \\n78: // SegmentFile represents the underlying file used to store a segment.\\n79: type SegmentFile interface {\\n80: \\tStat() (os.FileInfo, error)\\n81: \\tSync() error\\n82: \\tio.Writer\\n83: \\tio.Reader\\n84: \\tio.Closer\\n85: }\\n86: \\n87: // Segment represents a segment file.\\n88: type Segment struct {\\n89: \\tSegmentFile\\n90: \\tdir string\\n91: \\ti   int\\n92: }\\n93: \\n94: // Index returns the index of the segment.\\n95: func (s *Segment) Index() int {\\n96: \\treturn s.i\\n97: }\\n98: \\n99: // Dir returns the directory of the segment.\\n100: func (s *Segment) Dir() string {\\n101: \\treturn s.dir\\n102: }\\n103: \\n104: // CorruptionErr is an error that's returned when corruption is encountered.\\n105: type CorruptionErr struct {\\n106: \\tDir     string\\n107: \\tSegment int\\n108: \\tOffset  int64\\n109: \\tErr     error\\n110: }\\n111: \\n112: func (e *CorruptionErr) Error() string {\\n113: \\tif e.Segment < 0 {\\n114: \\t\\treturn fmt.Sprintf(\\\"corruption after %d bytes: %s\\\", e.Offset, e.Err)\\n115: \\t}\\n116: \\treturn fmt.Sprintf(\\\"corruption in segment %s at %d: %s\\\", SegmentName(e.Dir, e.Segment), e.Offset, e.Err)\\n117: }\\n118: \\n119: func (e *CorruptionErr) Unwrap() error {\\n120: \\treturn e.Err\\n121: }\\n122: \\n123: // OpenWriteSegment opens segment k in dir. The returned segment is ready for new appends.\\n124: func OpenWriteSegment(logger *slog.Logger, dir string, k int) (*Segment, error) {\\n125: \\tsegName := SegmentName(dir, k)\\n126: \\tf, err := os.OpenFile(segName, os.O_WRONLY|os.O_APPEND, 0o666)\\n127: \\tif err != nil {\\n128: \\t\\treturn nil, err\\n129: \\t}\\n130: \\tstat, err := f.Stat()\\n131: \\tif err != nil {\\n132: \\t\\tf.Close()\\n133: \\t\\treturn nil, err\\n134: \\t}\\n135: \\t// If the last page is torn, fill it with zeros.\\n136: \\t// In case it was torn after all records were written successfully, this\\n137: \\t// will just pad the page and everything will be fine.\\n138: \\t// If it was torn mid-record, a full read (which the caller should do anyway\\n139: \\t// to ensure integrity) will detect it as a corruption by the end.\\n140: \\tif d := stat.Size() % pageSize; It also ensures that torn writes never corrupt records\\n181: // beyond the most recent segment.\\n182: type WL struct {\\n183: \\tdir         string\\n184: \\tlogger      *slog.Logger\\n185: {\\n202: \\tfsyncDuration    prometheus.Summary\\n203: \\tpageFlushes      prometheus.Counter\\n204: \\tpageCompletions  prometheus.Counter\\n205: \\ttruncateFail     prometheus.Counter\\n206: \\tw.r.Unregister(w.recordBytesSaved)\\n232: }\\n233: \\n234: func newWLMetrics(w *WL, r prometheus.Registerer) *wlMetrics {\\n235: \\treturn &wlMetrics{\\n236: \\t\\tr: r,\\n237: \\t\\tfsyncDuration: NewSize returns a new write log over the given directory.\\n299: // New segments are created with the specified size.\\n300: func NewSize(logger *slog.Logger, reg prometheus.Registerer, dir string, segmentSize int, compress compression.Type) (*WL, error) {\\n301: \\tif segmentSize%pageSize != 0 {\\n302: \\t\\treturn nil, errors.New(\\\"invalid segment size\\\")\\n303: \\t}\\n304: \\tif err := os.MkdirAll(dir, 0o777); err != nil {\\n305: \\t\\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\\\"create dir: %w\\\", err)\\n306: \\t}\\n307: \\tif logger == nil {\\n308: \\t\\tlogger = promslog.NewNopLogger()\\n309: \\t}\\n310: \\n311: \\tw := &WL{\\n312: \\t\\tdir:         dir,\\n313: \\t\\tlogger:      logger,\\n314: \\t\\tsegmentSize: segmentSize,\\n315: \\t\\tpage:        &page{},\\n316: \\t\\tactorc: \\n350: \\treturn w, nil\\n351: }\\n352: \\n353: // Open an existing WAL.\\n354: func Open(logger *slog.Logger, dir string) (*WL, error) {\\n355: \\tif logger == nil {\\n356: \\t\\tlogger = promslog.NewNopLogger()\\n357: \\t}\\n358: \\n359: \\tw := &WL{\\n360: \\t\\tdir:    dir,\\n361: \\t\\tlogger: logger,\\n362: \\t}\\n363: \\treturn w, nil\\n364: }\\n365: \\n366: // CompressionType WAL.\\n372: func (w *WL) Dir() string {\\n373: \\treturn w.dir\\n374: }\\n375: \\n376: func (w *WL) SetWriteNotified(wn WriteNotified) {\\n377: \\tw.WriteNotified = wn\\n378: }\\n379: \\n380: func (w *WL) run() {\\n381: Loop:\\n382: \\tfor {\\n383: \\t\\tselect {\\n384: \\t\\tcase f := <-w.actorc:\\n385: \\t\\t\\tf()\\n386: \\t\\tcase donec := <-w.stopc:\\n387: \\t\\t\\tclose(w.actorc)\\n388: \\t\\t\\tdefer close(donec)\\n389: \\t\\t\\tbreak Loop\\n390: \\t\\t}\\n391: \\t}\\n392: \\t// Drain and process any remaining functions.\\n393: \\tfor f := range w.actorc {\\n394: \\t\\tf()\\n395: \\t}\\n396: }\\n397: \\n398: // Repair attempts to repair the WAL based on the error.\\n399: // It discards all data after the corruption.\\n400: func (w *WL) Repair(origErr error) error {\\n401: \\t// We could probably have a mode that only discards torn records right around\\n402: \\t// the corruption to preserve as data much as possible.\\n403: \\t// But that's not generally applicable if the records have any kind of causality.\\n404: \\t// Maybe as an extra mode in the future if mid-WAL corruptions become\\n405: \\t// a frequent concern.\\n406: \\tvar cerr *CorruptionErr\\n407: \\tif !errors.As(origErr, &cerr) {\\n408: \\t\\treturn fmt.Errorf(\\\"cannot handle error: %w\\\", origErr)\\n409: \\t}\\n410: \\tif cerr.Segment < 0 {\\n411: \\t\\treturn errors.New(\\\"corruption error does not specify position\\\")\\n412: \\t}\\n413: \\tw.logger.Warn(\\\"Starting corruption repair\\\",\\n414: \\t\\t\\\"segment\\\", cerr.Segment, \\\"offset\\\", cerr.Offset)\\n415: \\n416: \\t// All segments behind the corruption can no longer be used.\\n417: \\tsegs, err := listSegments(w.Dir())\\n418: \\tif err != nil {\\n419: \\t\\treturn fmt.Errorf(\\\"list segments: %w\\\", err)\\n420: \\t}\\n421: \\tw.logger.Warn(\\\"Deleting all segments newer than corrupted segment\\\", \\\"segment\\\", cerr.Segment)\\n422: \\n423: \\tfor _, s := range segs {\\n424: \\t\\tif w.segment.i == s.index {\\n425: \\t\\t\\t// The active segment needs to be removed,\\n426: \\t\\t\\t// close it first (Windows!). Can be closed safely\\n427: \\t\\t\\t// as we set the current segment to repaired file\\n428: \\t\\t\\t// below.\\n429: \\t\\t\\tif err := w.segment.Close(); err != nil {\\n430: \\t\\t\\t\\treturn fmt.Errorf(\\\"close active segment: %w\\\", err)\\n431: \\t\\t\\t}\\n432: \\t\\t}\\n433: \\t\\tif s.index <= cerr.Segment {\\n434: \\t\\t\\tcontinue\\n435: \\t\\t}\\n436: \\t\\tif err := os.Remove(filepath.Join(w.Dir(), s.name)); err != nil {\\n437: \\t\\t\\treturn fmt.Errorf(\\\"delete segment:%v: %w\\\", s.index, err)\\n438: \\t\\t}\\n439: \\t}\\n440: \\t// Regardless of the corruption offset, no record reaches into the previous segment.\\n441: \\t// So we can safely repair the WAL by removing the segment and re-inserting all\\n442: \\t// its records up to the corruption.\\n443: \\tw.logger.Warn(\\\"Rewrite corrupted segment\\\", \\\"segment\\\", cerr.Segment)\\n444: \\n445: \\tfn := SegmentName(w.Dir(), cerr.Segment)\\n446: \\ttmpfn := fn + \\\".repair\\\"\\n447: \\n448: \\tif err := fileutil.Rename(fn, tmpfn); err != nil {\\n449: \\t\\treturn err\\n450: \\t}\\n451: \\t// Create a clean segment and make it the active one.\\n452: \\ts, err := CreateSegment(w.Dir(), cerr.Segment)\\n453: \\tif err != nil {\\n454: \\t\\treturn err\\n455: \\t}\\n456: \\tif err := w.setSegment(s); err != nil {\\n457: \\t\\treturn err\\n458: \\t}\\n459: \\n460: \\tf, err := os.Open(tmpfn)\\n461: \\tif err != nil {\\n462: \\t\\treturn fmt.Errorf(\\\"open segment: %w\\\", err)\\n463: \\t}\\n464: \\tdefer f.Close()\\n465: \\n466: \\tr := NewReader(bufio.NewReader(f))\\n467: \\n468: \\tfor r.Next() {\\n469: \\t\\t// Add records only up to the where the error was.\\n470: \\t\\tif r.Offset() >= cerr.Offset {\\n471: \\t\\t\\tbreak\\n472: \\t\\t}\\n473: \\t\\tif err := w.Log(r.Record()); err != nil {\\n474: \\t\\t\\treturn fmt.Errorf(\\\"insert record: %w\\\", err)\\n475: \\t\\t}\\n476: \\t}\\n477: \\t// We expect an error here from r.Err(), so nothing to handle.\\n478: \\n479: \\t// We need to pad to the end of the last page in the repaired segment\\n480: \\tif err := w.flushPage(true); err != nil {\\n481: \\t\\treturn fmt.Errorf(\\\"flush page in repair: %w\\\", err)\\n482: \\t}\\n483: \\n484: \\t// We explicitly close even when there is a defer for Windows to be\\n485: \\t// able to delete it. The defer is in place to close it in-case there\\n486: \\t// are errors above.\\n487: \\tif err := f.Close(); err != nil {\\n488: \\t\\treturn fmt.Errorf(\\\"close corrupted file: %w\\\", err)\\n489: \\t}\\n490: \\tif err := os.Remove(tmpfn); err != nil {\\n491: \\t\\treturn fmt.Errorf(\\\"delete corrupted segment: %w\\\", err)\\n492: \\t}\\n493: \\n494: \\t// Explicitly close the segment we just repaired to avoid issues with Windows.\\n495: \\ts.Close()\\n496: \\n497: \\t// We always want to start writing to a new Segment rather than an existing\\n498: \\t// Segment, which is handled by NewSize, but earlier in Repair we're deleting\\n499: \\t// all segments that come after the corrupted Segment. Recreate a new Segment here.\\n500: \\ts, err = CreateSegment(w.Dir(), cerr.Segment+1)\\n501: \\tif err != nil {\\n502: \\t\\treturn err\\n503: \\t}\\n504: \\treturn w.setSegment(s)\\n505: }\\n506: \\n507: // SegmentName builds a segment name for the directory.\\n508: func SegmentName(dir string, i int) string {\\n509: \\treturn filepath.Join(dir, fmt.Sprintf(\\\"%08d\\\", i))\\n510: }\\n511: \\n512: // NextSegment creates the next segment and closes the previous one asynchronously.\\n513: // It returns the file number of the new file.\\n514: func (w *WL) NextSegment() (int, error) {\\n515: \\tw.mtx.Lock()\\n516: \\tdefer w.mtx.Unlock()\\n517: \\treturn w.nextSegment(true)\\n518: }\\n519: \\n520: // NextSegmentSync creates the next segment and closes the previous one in sync.\\n521: // It returns the file number of the new file.\\n522: func (w *WL) NextSegmentSync() (int, error) {\\n523: \\tw.mtx.Lock()\\n524: \\tdefer w.mtx.Unlock()\\n525: \\treturn w.nextSegment(false)\\n526: }\\n527: \\n528: // nextSegment creates the next segment and closes the previous one.\\n529: // It returns the file number of the new file.\\n530: func (w *WL) nextSegment(async bool) (int, error) {\\n531: \\tif w.closed {\\n532: \\t\\treturn 0, errors.New(\\\"wlog is closed\\\")\\n533: \\t}\\n534: \\n535: \\t// Only flush the current page if it actually holds data.\\n536: \\tif w.page.alloc > 0 {\\n537: \\t\\tif err := w.flushPage(true); err != nil {\\n538: \\t\\t\\treturn 0, err\\n539: \\t\\t}\\n540: \\t}\\n541: \\tnext, err := CreateSegment(w.Dir(), w.segment.Index()+1)\\n542: \\tif err != nil {\\n543: \\t\\treturn 0, fmt.Errorf(\\\"create new segment file: %w\\\", err)\\n544: \\t}\\n545: \\tprev := w.segment\\n546: \\tif err := w.setSegment(next); err != nil {\\n547: \\t\\treturn 0, err\\n548: \\t}\\n549: \\n550: \\t// Don't block further writes by fsyncing the last segment.\\n551: \\tf := func() {\\n552: \\t\\tif err := w.fsync(prev); err != nil {\\n553: \\t\\t\\tw.logger.Error(\\\"sync previous segment\\\", \\\"err\\\", err)\\n554: \\t\\t}\\n555: \\t\\tif err := prev.Close(); err != nil {\\n556: \\t\\t\\tw.logger.Error(\\\"close previous segment\\\", \\\"err\\\", err)\\n557: \\t\\t}\\n558: \\t}\\n559: \\tif async {\\n560: \\t\\tw.actorc <- f\\n561: \\t} else {\\n562: \\t\\tf()\\n563: \\t}\\n564: \\treturn next.Index(), nil\\n565: }\\n566: \\n567: func (w *WL) setSegment(segment *Segment) error {\\n568: \\tw.segment = segment\\n569: \\n570: \\t// Correctly initialize donePages.\\n571: \\tstat, err := segment.Stat()\\n572: \\tif err != nil {\\n573: \\t\\treturn err\\n574: \\t}\\n575: \\tw.donePages = int(stat.Size() / pageSize)\\n576: \\tw.metrics.currentSegment.Set(float64(segment.Index()))\\n577: \\treturn nil\\n578: }\\n579: \\n580: // flushPage writes the new contents of the page to disk. If no more records will fit into\\n581: // the page, the remaining bytes will be set to zero and a new page will be started.\\n582: // If forceClear is true, this is enforced regardless of how many bytes are left in the page.\\n583: func (w *WL) flushPage(forceClear bool) error {\\n584: \\tw.metrics.pageFlushes.Inc()\\n585: \\n586: \\tp := w.page\\n587: \\tshouldClear := forceClear || p.full()\\n588: \\n589: \\t// No more data will fit into the page or an implicit clear.\\n590: \\t// Enqueue and clear it.\\n591: \\tif shouldClear {\\n592: \\t\\tp.alloc = pageSize // Write till end of page.\\n593: \\t}\\n594: \\n595: \\tn, err := w.segment.Write(p.buf[p.flushed:p.alloc])\\n596: \\tif err != nil {\\n597: \\t\\tp.flushed += n\\n598: \\t\\treturn err\\n599: \\t}\\n600: \\tp.flushed += n\\n601: \\n602: \\t// We flushed an entire page, prepare a new one.\\n603: \\tif shouldClear {\\n604: \\t\\tp.reset()\\n605: \\t\\tw.donePages++\\n606: \\t\\tw.metrics.pageCompletions.Inc()\\n607: \\t}\\n608: \\treturn nil\\n609: }\\n610: \\n611: // First Byte of header format:\\n612: //\\n613: //\\t[3 bits unallocated] [1 bit zstd compression flag] [1 bit snappy compression flag] [3 bit record type ]\\n614: const (\\n615: \\tsnappyMask  = 1 << 3\\n616: \\tzstdMask    = 1 << 4\\n617: \\trecTypeMask = snappyMask - 1\\n618: )\\n619: \\n620: type recType uint8\\n621: \\n622: const (\\n623: \\trecPageTerm recType = 0 // Rest of page is empty.\\n624: \\trecFull     recType = 1 // Full record.\\n625: \\trecFirst    recType = 2 // First fragment of a record.\\n626: \\trecMiddle   recType = 3 // Middle fragments of a record.\\n627: \\trecLast     recType = 4 // Final fragment of a record.\\n628: )\\n629: \\n630: func recTypeFromHeader(header byte) recType {\\n631: \\treturn recType(header & recTypeMask)\\n632: }\\n633: \\n634: func (t recType) String() string {\\n635: \\tswitch t {\\n636: \\tcase recPageTerm:\\n637: \\t\\treturn \\\"zero\\\"\\n638: \\tcase recFull:\\n639: \\t\\treturn \\\"full\\\"\\n640: \\tcase recFirst:\\n641: \\t\\treturn \\\"first\\\"\\n642: \\tcase recMiddle:\\n643: \\t\\treturn \\\"middle\\\"\\n644: \\tcase recLast:\\n645: \\t\\treturn \\\"last\\\"\\n646: \\tdefault:\\n647: \\t\\treturn \\\"<invalid>\\\"\\n648: \\t}\\n649: }\\n650: \\n651: func (w *WL) pagesPerSegment() int {\\n652: \\treturn w.segmentSize / pageSize\\n653: }\\n654: \\n655: // Log writes the records into the log.\\n656: // Multiple records can be passed at once to reduce writes and increase throughput.\\n657: func (w *WL) Log(recs ...[]byte) error {\\n658: \\tw.mtx.Lock()\\n659: \\tdefer w.mtx.Unlock()\\n660: \\t// Callers could just implement their own list record format but adding\\n661: \\t// a bit of extra logic here frees them from that overhead.\\n662: \\tfor i, r := range recs {\\n663: \\t\\tif err := w.log(r, i == len(recs)-1); err != nil {\\n664: \\t\\t\\tw.metrics.writesFailed.Inc()\\n665: \\t\\t\\treturn err\\n666: \\t\\t}\\n667: \\t}\\n668: \\treturn nil\\n669: }\\n670: \\n671: // log writes rec to the log and forces a flush of the current page if:\\n672: // - len(enc)\\n692: \\n693: \\t\\t// Even if the compression was applied, skip it, if there's no benefit\\n694: \\t\\t// in the WAL record size (we have a choice). For small records e.g. snappy\\n695: \\t\\t// compression can yield larger records than the uncompressed.\\n696: \\t\\tif savedBytes <= 0 {\\n697: \\t\\t\\tenc = rec\\n698: \\t\\t\\tfinalCompression = compression.None\\n699: \\t\\t\\tsavedBytes = 0\\n700: \\t\\t}\\n701: \\t\\tw.metrics.recordBytesSaved.WithLabelValues(w.compress).Add(float64(savedBytes))\\n702: \\t}\\n703: \\n704: \\t// If the record is too big to fit within the active page in the current\\n705: \\t// segment, terminate the active segment and advance to the next one.\\n706: \\t// This ensures that records do not cross segment boundaries.\\n707: \\tleft := w.page.remaining() - recordHeaderSize                                   // Free space in the active page.\\n708: \\tleft += (pageSize - recordHeaderSize) * (w.pagesPerSegment() - w.donePages - 1) // Free pages in the active segment.\\n709: \\n710: \\tif len(enc) > left {\\n711: \\t\\tif _, err := w.nextSegment(true); race\\n48: // with any other use of the crc32 package anywhere. p.alloc\\n64: }\\n65: \\n66: func (p *page) full() bool {\\n67: \\treturn pageSize-p.alloc < recordHeaderSize\\n68: }\\n69: \\n70: func (p *page) reset() {\\n71: \\tfor i := range p.buf {\\n72: \\t\\tp.buf[i] = 0\\n73: \\t}\\n74: \\tp.alloc = 0\\n75: \\tp.flushed = 0\\n76: }\\n77: \\n78: // SegmentFile represents the underlying file used to store a segment.\\n79: type SegmentFile interface {\\n80: \\tStat() (os.FileInfo, error)\\n81: \\tSync() error\\n82: \\tio.Writer\\n83: \\tio.Reader\\n84: \\tio.Closer\\n85: }\\n86: \\n87: // Segment represents a segment file.\\n88: type Segment struct {\\n89: \\tSegmentFile\\n90: \\tdir string\\n91: \\ti   int\\n92: }\\n93: \\n94: // Index returns the index of the segment.\\n95: func (s *Segment) Index() int {\\n96: \\treturn s.i\\n97: }\\n98: \\n99: // Dir returns the directory of the segment.\\n100: func (s *Segment) Dir() string {\\n101: \\treturn s.dir\\n102: }\\n103: \\n104: // CorruptionErr is an error that's returned when corruption is encountered.\\n105: type CorruptionErr struct {\\n106: \\tDir     string\\n107: \\tSegment int\\n108: \\tOffset  int64\\n109: \\tErr     error\\n110: }\\n111: \\n112: func (e *CorruptionErr) Error() string {\\n113: \\tif e.Segment < 0 {\\n114: \\t\\treturn fmt.Sprintf(\\\"corruption after %d bytes: %s\\\", e.Offset, e.Err)\\n115: \\t}\\n116: \\treturn fmt.Sprintf(\\\"corruption in segment %s at %d: %s\\\", SegmentName(e.Dir, e.Segment), e.Offset, e.Err)\\n117: }\\n118: \\n119: func (e *CorruptionErr) Unwrap() error {\\n120: \\treturn e.Err\\n121: }\\n122: \\n123: // OpenWriteSegment opens segment k in dir. The returned segment is ready for new appends.\\n124: func OpenWriteSegment(logger *slog.Logger, dir string, k int) (*Segment, error) {\\n125: \\tsegName := SegmentName(dir, k)\\n126: \\tf, err := os.OpenFile(segName, os.O_WRONLY|os.O_APPEND, 0o666)\\n127: \\tif err != nil {\\n128: \\t\\treturn nil, err\\n129: \\t}\\n130: \\tstat, err := f.Stat()\\n131: \\tif err != nil {\\n132: \\t\\tf.Close()\\n133: \\t\\treturn nil, err\\n134: \\t}\\n135: \\t// If the last page is torn, fill it with zeros.\\n136: \\t// In case it was torn after all records were written successfully, this\\n137: \\t// will just pad the page and everything will be fine.\\n138: \\t// If it was torn mid-record, a full read (which the caller should do anyway\\n139: \\t// to ensure integrity) will detect it as a corruption by the end.\\n140: \\tif d := stat.Size() % pageSize; \\tw.r.Unregister(w.recordBytesSaved)\\n232: }\\n233: \\n234: func newWLMetrics(w *WL, r prometheus.Registerer) *wlMetrics {\\n235: \\treturn &wlMetrics{\\n236: \\t\\tr: r,\\n237: \\t\\tfsyncDuration: \\t}\\n396: }\\n397: \\n398: // Repair attempts to repair the WAL based on the error.\\n399: // It discards all data after the corruption.\\n400: func (w *WL) Repair(origErr error) error {\\n401: \\t// We could probably have a mode that only discards torn records right around\\n402: \\t// the corruption to preserve as data much as possible.\\n403: \\t// But that's not generally applicable if the records have any kind of causality.\\n404: \\t// Maybe as an extra mode in the future if mid-WAL corruptions become\\n405: \\t// a frequent concern.\\n406: \\tvar cerr *CorruptionErr\\n407: \\tif !errors.As(origErr, &cerr) {\\n408: \\t\\treturn fmt.Errorf(\\\"cannot handle error: %w\\\", origErr)\\n409: \\t}\\n410: \\tif cerr.Segment < 0 {\\n411: \\t\\treturn errors.New(\\\"corruption error does not specify position\\\")\\n412: \\t}\\n413: \\tw.logger.Warn(\\\"Starting corruption repair\\\",\\n414: \\t\\t\\\"segment\\\", cerr.Segment, \\\"offset\\\", cerr.Offset)\\n415: \\n416: \\t// All segments behind the corruption can no longer be used.\\n417: \\tsegs, err := listSegments(w.Dir())\\n418: \\tif err != nil {\\n419: \\t\\treturn fmt.Errorf(\\\"list segments: %w\\\", err)\\n420: \\t}\\n421: \\tw.logger.Warn(\\\"Deleting all segments newer than corrupted segment\\\", \\\"segment\\\", cerr.Segment)\\n422: \\n423: \\tfor _, s := range segs {\\n424: \\t\\tif w.segment.i == s.index {\\n425: \\t\\t\\t// The active segment needs to be removed,\\n426: \\t\\t\\t// close it first (Windows!). Can be closed safely\\n427: \\t\\t\\t// as we set the current segment to repaired file\\n428: \\t\\t\\t// below.\\n429: \\t\\t\\tif err := w.segment.Close(); err != nil {\\n430: \\t\\t\\t\\treturn fmt.Errorf(\\\"close active segment: %w\\\", err)\\n431: \\t\\t\\t}\\n432: \\t\\t}\\n433: \\t\\tif s.index <= cerr.Segment {\\n434: \\t\\t\\tcontinue\\n435: \\t\\t}\\n436: \\t\\tif err := os.Remove(filepath.Join(w.Dir(), s.name)); err != nil {\\n437: \\t\\t\\treturn fmt.Errorf(\\\"delete segment:%v: %w\\\", s.index, err)\\n438: \\t\\t}\\n439: \\t}\\n440: \\t// Regardless of the corruption offset, no record reaches into the previous segment.\\n441: \\t// So we can safely repair the WAL by removing the segment and re-inserting all\\n442: \\t// its records up to the corruption.\\n443: \\tw.logger.Warn(\\\"Rewrite corrupted segment\\\", \\\"segment\\\", cerr.Segment)\\n444: \\n445: \\tfn := SegmentName(w.Dir(), cerr.Segment)\\n446: \\ttmpfn := fn + \\\".repair\\\"\\n447: \\n448: \\tif err := fileutil.Rename(fn, tmpfn); err != nil {\\n474: \\t\\t\\treturn fmt.Errorf(\\\"insert record: %w\\\", err)\\n475: \\t\\t}\\n476: \\t}\\n477: \\t// We expect an error here from r.Err(), so nothing to handle.\\n478: \\n479: \\t// We need to pad to the end of the last page in the repaired segment\\n480: \\tif err := w.flushPage(true); err != nil {\\n481: \\t\\treturn fmt.Errorf(\\\"flush page in repair: %w\\\", err)\\n482: \\t}\\n483: \\n484: \\t// We explicitly close even when there is a defer for Windows to be\\n485: \\t// able to delete it. The defer is in place to close it in-case there\\n486: \\t// are errors above.\\n487: \\tif err := f.Close(); err != nil {\\n488: \\t\\treturn fmt.Errorf(\\\"close corrupted file: %w\\\", err)\\n489: \\t}\\n490: \\tif err := os.Remove(tmpfn); err != nil {\\n491: \\t\\treturn fmt.Errorf(\\\"delete corrupted segment: %w\\\", err)\\n492: \\t}\\n493: \\n494: \\t// Explicitly close the segment we just repaired to avoid issues with Windows.\\n495: \\ts.Close()\\n496: \\n497: \\t// We always want to start writing to a new Segment rather than an existing\\n498: \\t// Segment, which is handled by NewSize, but earlier in Repair we're deleting\\n499: \\t// all segments that come after the corrupted Segment. Recreate a new Segment here.\\n500: \\ts, err = CreateSegment(w.Dir(), cerr.Segment+1)\\n501: \\tif err != nil {\\n502: \\t\\treturn err\\n503: \\t}\\n504: \\treturn w.setSegment(s)\\n505: }\\n506: \\n507: // SegmentName builds a segment name for the directory.\\n508: func SegmentName(dir string, i int) string {\\n509: \\treturn filepath.Join(dir, fmt.Sprintf(\\\"%08d\\\", i))\\n510: }\\n511: \\n512: // NextSegment creates the next segment and closes the previous one asynchronously.\\n513: // It returns the file number of the new file.\\n514: func (w *WL) NextSegment() (int, error) {\\n515: \\tw.mtx.Lock()\\n516: \\tdefer w.mtx.Unlock()\\n517: \\treturn w.nextSegment(true)\\n518: }\\n519: \\n520: // NextSegmentSync creates the next segment and closes the previous one in sync.\\n521: // It returns the file number of the new file.\\n522: func (w *WL) NextSegmentSync() (int, error) {\\n523: \\tw.mtx.Lock()\\n524: \\tdefer w.mtx.Unlock()\\n525: \\treturn w.nextSegment(false)\\n526: }\\n527: \\n528: // nextSegment creates the next segment and closes the previous one.\\n529: // It returns the file number of the new file.\\n530: func (w *WL) nextSegment(async bool) (int, error) {\\n531: \\tif w.closed {\\n532: \\t\\treturn 0, errors.New(\\\"wlog is closed\\\")\\n533: \\t}\\n534: \\n535: \\t// Only flush the current page if it actually holds data.\\n536: \\tif w.page.alloc > 0 {\\n537: \\t\\tif err := w.flushPage(true); err != nil {\\n547: \\t\\treturn 0, err\\n548: \\t}\\n549: \\n550: \\t// Don't block further writes by fsyncing the last segment.\\n551: \\tf := func() {\\n552: \\t\\tif err := w.fsync(prev); err != nil {\\n553: \\t\\t\\tw.logger.Error(\\\"sync previous segment\\\", \\\"err\\\", err)\\n554: \\t\\t}\\n555: \\t\\tif err := prev.Close(); err != nil {\\n556: \\t\\t\\tw.logger.Error(\\\"close previous segment\\\", \\\"err\\\", err)\\n557: \\t\\t}\\n558: \\t}\\n559: \\tif async {\\n560: \\t\\tw.actorc <- f\\n561: \\t} else {\\n562: \\t\\tf()\\n563: \\t}\\n564: \\treturn next.Index(), nil\\n565: }\\n566: \\n567: func (w *WL) setSegment(segment *Segment) error {\\n568: \\tw.segment = segment\\n569: \\n570: \\t// Correctly initialize donePages.\\n571: \\tstat, err := segment.Stat()\\n572: \\tif err != nil {\\n573: \\t\\treturn err\\n574: \\t}\\n575: \\tw.donePages = int(stat.Size() / pageSize)\\n576: \\tw.metrics.currentSegment.Set(float64(segment.Index()))\\n577: \\treturn nil\\n578: }\\n579: \\n580: // flushPage writes the new contents of the page to disk. If no more records will fit into\\n581: // the page, the remaining bytes will be set to zero and a new page will be started.\\n582: // If forceClear is true, this is enforced regardless of how many bytes are left in the page.\\n583: func (w *WL) flushPage(forceClear bool) error {\\n584: \\tw.metrics.pageFlushes.Inc()\\n585: \\n586: \\tp := w.page\\n587: \\tshouldClear := forceClear || p.full()\\n588: \\n589: \\t// No more data will fit into the page or an implicit clear.\\n590: \\t// Enqueue and clear it.\\n591: \\tif shouldClear {\\n592: \\t\\tp.alloc = pageSize // Write till end of page.\\n593: \\t}\\n594: \\n595: \\tn, err := w.segment.Write(p.buf[p.flushed:p.alloc])\\n596: \\tif err != nil {\\n597: \\t\\tp.flushed += n\\n598: \\t\\treturn err\\n599: \\t}\\n600: \\tp.flushed += n\\n601: \\n602: \\t// We flushed an entire page, prepare a new one.\\n603: \\tif shouldClear {\\n604: \\t\\tp.reset()\\n605: \\t\\tw.donePages++\\n606: \\t\\tw.metrics.pageCompletions.Inc()\\n607: \\t}\\n608: \\treturn nil\\n609: }\\n610: \\n611: // First Byte of header format:\\n612: //\\n613: //\\t[3 bits unallocated] [1 bit zstd compression flag] [1 bit snappy compression flag] [3 bit record type ]\\n614: const (\\n615: \\tsnappyMask  = 1 << 3\\n616: \\tzstdMask    = 1 << 4\\n617: \\trecTypeMask = snappyMask - 1\\n618: )\\n619: \\n620: type recType uint8\\n621: \\n622: const (\\n623: \\trecPageTerm recType = 0 // Rest of page is empty.\\n624: \\trecFull     recType = 1 // Full record.\\n625: \\trecFirst    recType = 2 // First fragment of a record.\\n626: \\trecMiddle   recType = 3 // Middle fragments of a record.\\n627: \\trecLast     recType = 4 // Final fragment of a record.\\n628: )\\n629: \\n630: func recTypeFromHeader(header byte) recType {\\n631: \\treturn recType(header & recTypeMask)\\n632: }\\n633: \\n634: func (t recType) String() string {\\n635: \\tswitch t {\\n636: \\tcase recPageTerm:\\n637: \\t\\treturn \\\"zero\\\"\\n638: \\tcase recFull:\\n639: \\t\\treturn \\\"full\\\"\\n640: \\tcase recFirst:\\n641: \\t\\treturn \\\"first\\\"\\n642: \\tcase recMiddle:\\n643: \\t\\treturn \\\"middle\\\"\\n644: \\tcase recLast:\\n645: \\t\\treturn \\\"last\\\"\\n646: \\tdefault:\\n647: \\t\\treturn \\\"<invalid>\\\"\\n648: \\t}\\n649: }\\n650: \\n651: func (w *WL) pagesPerSegment() int {\\n652: \\treturn w.segmentSize / pageSize\\n653: }\\n654: \\n655: // Log writes the records into the log.\\n656: // Multiple records can be passed at once to reduce writes and increase throughput.\\n657: func (w *WL) Log(recs ...[]byte) error {\\n658: \\tw.mtx.Lock()\\n659: \\tdefer w.mtx.Unlock()\\n660: \\t// Callers could just implement their own list record format but adding\\n661: \\t// a bit of extra logic here frees them from that overhead.\\n662: \\tfor i, r := range recs {\\n663: \\t\\tif err := w.log(r, i == len(recs)-1); err != nil {\\n664: \\t\\t\\tw.metrics.writesFailed.Inc()\\n665: \\t\\t\\treturn err\\n666: \\t\\t}\\n667: \\t}\\n668: \\treturn nil\\n669: }\\n670: \\n671: // log writes rec to the log and forces a flush of the current page if:\\n672: // - the final record of a batch\\n673: // - the record is bigger than the page size\\n674: // - the current page is full.\\n675: func (w *WL) log(rec []byte, final bool) error {\\n676: \\t// When the last page flush failed the page will remain full.\\n677: \\t// When the page is full, need to flush it before trying to add more records to it.\\n678: \\tif w.page.full() {\\n679: \\t\\tif err := w.flushPage(true); err != nil {\\n680: \\t\\t\\treturn err\\n681: \\t\\t}\\n682: \\t}\\n683: \\n684: \\t// Compress the record before calculating if a new segment is needed.\\n685: \\tfinalCompression := w.compress\\n686: \\tenc, err := compression.Encode(w.compress, rec, w.cEnc)\\n687: \\tif err != nil {\\n688: \\t\\treturn err\\n689: \\t}\\n690: \\tif w.compress != compression.None {\\n691: \\t\\tsavedBytes := len(rec) - len(enc)\\n692: \\n693: \\t\\t// Even if the compression was applied, skip it, if there's no benefit\\n694: \\t\\t// in the WAL record size (we have a choice). For small records e.g. snappy\\n695: \\t\\t// compression can yield larger records than the uncompressed.\\n696: \\t\\tif savedBytes <= 0 {\\n697: \\t\\t\\tenc = rec\\n698: \\t\\t\\tfinalCompression = compression.None\\n699: \\t\\t\\tsavedBytes = 0\\n700: \\t\\t}\\n701: \\t\\tw.metrics.recordBytesSaved.WithLabelValues(w.compress).Add(float64(savedBytes))\\n702: \\t}\\n703: \\n704: \\t// If the record is too big to fit within the active page in the current\\n705: \\t// segment, terminate the active segment and advance to the next one.\\n706: \\t// This ensures that records do not cross segment boundaries.\\n707: \\tleft := w.page.remaining() - recordHeaderSize                                   // Free space in the active page.\\n708: \\tleft += (pageSize - recordHeaderSize) * (w.pagesPerSegment() - w.donePages - 1) // Free pages in the active segment.\\n709: \\n710: \\tif len(enc) > left {\\n711: \\t\\tif _, err := w.nextSegment(true); i == 0 || len(enc) > 0; i++ {\\n719: \\t\\tp := w.page\\n720: \\n721: \\t\\t// Find how much of the record we can fit into the page.\\n722: \\t\\tvar (\\n723: \\t\\t\\tl    = min(len(enc), (pageSize-p.alloc)-recordHeaderSize)\\n724: \\t\\t\\tpart = enc[:l]\\n725: \\t\\t\\tbuf  = p.buf[p.alloc:]\\n726: \\t\\t\\ttyp  recType\\n727: \\t\\t)\\n728: \\n729: \\t\\tswitch {\\n730: \\t\\tcase i == 0 && len(part) == len(enc):\\n731: \\t\\t\\ttyp = recFull\\n732: \\t\\tcase len(part) == len(enc):\\n733: \\t\\t\\ttyp = recLast\\n734: \\t\\tcase i == 0:\\n735: \\t\\t\\ttyp = recFirst\\n736: \\t\\tdefault:\\n737: \\t\\t\\ttyp = recMiddle\\n738: \\t\\t}\\n739: \\n740: \\t\\tif finalCompression != compression.None {\\n741: \\t\\t\\tswitch finalCompression {\\n742: \\t\\t\\tcase compression.Snappy:\\n743: \\t\\t\\t\\ttyp |= snappyMask\\n744: \\t\\t\\tcase compression.Zstd:\\n745: \\t\\t\\t\\ttyp |= zstdMask\\n746: \\t\\t\\tdefault:\\n747: \\t\\t\\t\\treturn fmt.Errorf(\\\"unsupported compression type: %v\\\", finalCompression)\\n748: \\t\\t\\t}\\n749: \\t\\t}\\n750: \\n751: \\t\\tbuf[0] = byte(typ)\\n752: \\t\\tcrc := crc32.Checksum(part, castagnoliTable)\\n753: \\t\\tbinary.BigEndian.PutUint16(buf[1:], uint16(len(part)))\\n754: \\t\\tbinary.BigEndian.PutUint32(buf[3:], crc)\\n755: \\n756: \\t\\tcopy(buf[recordHeaderSize:], part)\\n757: \\t\\tp.alloc += len(part) + recordHeaderSize\\n758: \\n759: \\t\\tw.metrics.recordPartWrites.Inc()\\n760: \\t\\tw.metrics.recordPartBytes.Add(float64(len(part) + recordHeaderSize))\\n761: \\n762: \\t\\tif w.page.full() {\\n763: \\t\\t\\tif err := w.flushPage(true); Thus we initialize it\n49: // before.\n50: var castagnoliTable = crc32.MakeTable(crc32.Castagnoli)\n51: \n52: // page is an in memory buffer used to batch disk writes.\n53: // Records bigger than the page size are split and flushed separately.\n54: // A flush is triggered when a single records doesn't fit the page size or\n55: // when the next record can't fit in the remaining free page space.\n56: type page struct {\n57: \talloc   int\n58: \tflushed int\n59: \tbuf     [pageSize]byte\n60: }\n61: \n62: func (p *page) remaining() int {\n63: \treturn pageSize - The returned segment is ready for new appends.\n124: func OpenWriteSegment(logger *slog.Logger, dir string, k int) (*Segment, error) {\n125: \tsegName := SegmentName(dir, k)\n126: \tf, err := os.OpenFile(segName, os.O_WRONLY|os.O_APPEND, 0o666)\n127: \tif err != nil {\n128: \t\treturn nil, err\n129: \t}\n130: \tstat, err := f.Stat()\n131: \tif err != nil {\n132: \t\tf.Close()\n133: \t\treturn nil, err\n134: \t}\n135: \t// If the last page is torn, fill it with zeros.\n136: \t// In case it was torn after all records were written successfully, this\n137: \t// will just pad the page and everything will be fine.\n138: \t// If it was torn mid-record, a full read (which the caller should do anyway\n139: \t// to ensure integrity) will detect it as a corruption by the end.\n140: \tif d := stat.Size() % pageSize; d != 0 {\n141: \t\tlogger.Warn(\"Last page of the wlog is torn, filling it with zeros\", \"segment\", segName)\n142: \t\tif _, err := f.Write(make([]byte, pageSize-d)); err != nil {\n143: \t\t\tf.Close()\n144: \t\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"zero-pad torn page: %w\", err)\n145: \t\t}\n146: \t}\n147: \treturn &Segment{SegmentFile: f, i: k, dir: dir}, nil\n148: }\n149: \n150: // CreateSegment creates a new segment k in dir.\n151: func CreateSegment(dir string, k int) (*Segment, error) {\n152: \tf, err := os.OpenFile(SegmentName(dir, k), os.O_WRONLY|os.O_CREATE|os.O_APPEND, 0o666)\n153: \tif err != nil {\n154: \t\treturn nil, err\n155: \t}\n156: \treturn &Segment{SegmentFile: f, i: k, dir: dir}, nil\n157: }\n158: \n159: // OpenReadSegment opens the segment with the given filename.\n160: func OpenReadSegment(fn string) (*Segment, error) {\n161: \tk, err := strconv.Atoi(filepath.Base(fn))\n162: \tif err != nil {\n163: \t\treturn nil, errors.New(\"not a valid filename\")\n164: \t}\n165: \tf, err := os.Open(fn)\n166: \tif err != nil {\n167: \t\treturn nil, err\n168: \t}\n169: \treturn &Segment{SegmentFile: f, i: k, dir: filepath.Dir(fn)}, nil\n170: }\n171: \n172: // WL is a write log that stores records in segment files.\n173: // It must be read from start to end once before logging new data.\n174: // If an error occurs during read, the repair procedure must be called\n175: // before it's safe to do further writes.\n176: //\n177: // Segments are written to in pages of 32KB, with records possibly split\n178: // across page boundaries.\n179: // Records are never split across segments to allow full segments to be\n180: // safely truncated. It also ensures that torn writes never corrupt records\n181: // beyond the most recent segment.\n182: type WL struct {\n183: \tdir         string\n184: \tlogger      *slog.Logger\n185: \tsegmentSize int\n186: \tmtx         sync.RWMutex\n187: \tsegment     *Segment // Active segment.\n188: \tdonePages   int      // Pages written to the segment.\n189: \tpage        *page    // Active page.\n190: \tstopc       chan chan struct{}\n191: \tactorc      chan func()\n192: \tclosed      bool // To allow calling Close() more than once without blocking.\n193: \tcompress    compression.Type\n194: \tcEnc        compression.EncodeBuffer\n195: \n196: \tWriteNotified WriteNotified\n197: \n198: \tmetrics *wlMetrics\n199: }\n200: \n201: type wlMetrics struct {\n202: \tfsyncDuration    prometheus.Summary\n203: \tpageFlushes      prometheus.Counter\n204: \tpageCompletions  prometheus.Counter\n205: \ttruncateFail     prometheus.Counter\n206: \ttruncateTotal    prometheus.Counter\n207: \tcurrentSegment   prometheus.Gauge\n208: \twritesFailed     prometheus.Counter\n209: \twalFileSize      prometheus.GaugeFunc\n210: \trecordPartWrites prometheus.Counter\n211: \trecordPartBytes  prometheus.Counter\n212: \trecordBytesSaved *prometheus.CounterVec\n213: \n214: \tr prometheus.Registerer\n215: }\n216: \n217: func (w *wlMetrics) Unregister() {\n218: \tif w.r == nil {\n219: \t\treturn\n220: \t}\n221: \tw.r.Unregister(w.fsyncDuration)\n222: \tw.r.Unregister(w.pageFlushes)\n223: \tw.r.Unregister(w.pageCompletions)\n224: \tw.r.Unregister(w.truncateFail)\n225: \tw.r.Unregister(w.truncateTotal)\n226: \tw.r.Unregister(w.currentSegment)\n227: \tw.r.Unregister(w.writesFailed)\n228: \tw.r.Unregister(w.walFileSize)\n229: \tw.r.Unregister(w.recordPartWrites)\n230: \tw.r.Unregister(w.recordPartBytes)\n231: \tw.r.Unregister(w.recordBytesSaved)\n232: }\n233: \n234: func newWLMetrics(w *WL, r prometheus.Registerer) *wlMetrics {\n235: \treturn &wlMetrics{\n236: directory.\n294: func New(logger *slog.Logger, reg prometheus.Registerer, dir string, compress compression.Type) (*WL, error) {\n295: \treturn NewSize(logger, reg, dir, DefaultSegmentSize, compress)\n296: }\n297: \n298: // NewSize returns a new write log over the given directory.\n299: // New segments are created with the specified size.\n300: func NewSize(logger *slog.Logger, reg prometheus.Registerer, dir string, segmentSize int, compress compression.Type) (*WL, error) {\n301: \tif segmentSize%pageSize != 0 {\n302: \t\treturn nil, errors.New(\"invalid segment size\")\n303: \t}\n304: \tif err := os.MkdirAll(dir, 0o777); err != nil {\n305: \t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"create dir: %w\", err)\n306: \t}\n307: \tif logger == nil {\n308: \t\tlogger = promslog.NewNopLogger()\n309: \t}\n310: \n311: \tw := &WL{\n312: \t\tdir:         dir,\n313: \t\tlogger:      logger,\n314: \t\tsegmentSize: segmentSize,\n315: \t\tpage:        &page{},\n316: \t\tactorc:      make(chan func(), 100),\n317: \t\tstopc:       make(chan chan struct{}),\n318: \t\tcompress:    compress,\n319: \t\tcEnc:        compression.NewSyncEncodeBuffer(),\n320: \t}\n321: \tprefix := \"prometheus_tsdb_wal_\"\n322: \tif filepath.Base(dir) == WblDirName {\n323: \t\tprefix = \"prometheus_tsdb_out_of_order_wbl_\"\n324: \t}\n325: \tw.metrics = newWLMetrics(w, prometheus.WrapRegistererWithPrefix(prefix, reg))\n326: \n327: \t_, last, err := Segments(w.Dir())\n328: \tif err != nil {\n329: \t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"get segment range: %w\", err)\n330: \t}\n331: \n332: \t// Index of the Segment we want to open and write to.\n333: \twriteSegmentIndex := 0\n334: \t// If some segments already exist create one with a higher index than the last segment.\n335: \tif last != -1 {\n336: \t\twriteSegmentIndex = last + 1\n337: \t}\n338: \n339: \tsegment, err := CreateSegment(w.Dir(), writeSegmentIndex)\n340: \tif err != nil {\n341: \t\treturn nil, err\n342: \t}\n343: \n344: \tif err := w.setSegment(segment); err != nil {\n345: \t\treturn nil, err\n346: \t}\n347: \n348: \tgo w.run()\n349: \n350: \treturn w, nil\n351: }\n352: \n353: // Open an existing WAL.\n354: func Open(logger *slog.Logger, dir string) (*WL, error) {\n355: \tif logger == nil {\n356: \t\tlogger = promslog.NewNopLogger()\n357: \t}\n358: \n359: \tw := &WL{\n360: \t\tdir:    dir,\n361: \t\tlogger: logger,\n362: \t}\n363: \treturn w, nil\n364: }\n365: \n366: // CompressionType returns if compression is enabled on this WAL.\n367: func (w *WL) CompressionType() compression.Type {\n368: \treturn w.compress\n369: }\n370: \n371: // Dir returns the directory of the WAL.\n372: func (w *WL) Dir() string {\n373: \treturn w.dir\n374: }\n375: \n376: func (w *WL) SetWriteNotified(wn WriteNotified) {\n377: \tw.WriteNotified = wn\n378: }\n379: \n380: func (w *WL) run() {\n381: Loop:\n382: \tfor {\n383: \t\tselect {\n384: \t\tcase f := <-w.actorc:\n385: \t\t\tf()\n386: \t\tcase donec := <-w.stopc:\n387: \t\t\tclose(w.actorc)\n388: \t\t\tdefer close(donec)\n389: \t\t\tbreak Loop\n390: \t\t}\n391: \t}\n392: \t// Drain and process any remaining functions.\n393: \tfor f := range w.actorc {\n394: \t\tf()\n395: \t}\n396: }\n397: \n398: // Repair attempts to repair the WAL based on the error.\n399: // It discards all data after the corruption.\n400: func (w *WL) Repair(origErr error) error {\n401: \t// We could probably have a mode that only discards torn records right around\n402: \t// the corruption to preserve as data much as possible.\n403: \t// But that's not generally applicable if the records have any kind of causality.\n404: \t// Maybe as an extra mode in the future if mid-WAL corruptions become\n405: \t// a frequent concern.\n406: \tvar cerr *CorruptionErr\n407: \tif !errors.As(origErr, &cerr) {\n408: \t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"cannot handle error: %w\", origErr)\n409: \t}\n410: \tif cerr.Segment < 0 {\n411: \t\treturn errors.New(\"corruption error does not specify position\")\n412: \t}\n413: \tw.logger.Warn(\"Starting corruption repair\",\n414: \t\t\"segment\", cerr.Segment, \"offset\", cerr.Offset)\n415: \n416: \t// All segments behind the corruption can no longer be used.\n417: \tsegs, err := listSegments(w.Dir())\n418: \tif err != nil {\n419: \t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"list segments: %w\", err)\n420: \t}\n421: \tw.logger.Warn(\"Deleting all segments newer than corrupted segment\", \"segment\", cerr.Segment)\n422: \n423: \tfor _, s := range segs {\n424: \t\tif w.segment.i == s.index {\n425: \t\t\t// The active segment needs to be removed,\n426: \t\t\t// close it first (Windows!). Can be closed safely\n427: \t\t\t// as we set the current segment to repaired file\n428: \t\t\t// below.\n429: \t\t\tif err := w.segment.Close(); err != nil {\n430: \t\t\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"close active segment: %w\", err)\n431: \t\t\t}\n432: \t\t}\n433: \t\tif s.index <= cerr.Segment {\n434: \t\t\tcontinue\n435: \t\t}\n436: \t\tif err := os.Remove(filepath.Join(w.Dir(), s.name)); err != nil {\n437: \t\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"delete segment:%v: %w\", s.index, err)\n438: \t\t}\n439: \t}\n440: \t// Regardless of the corruption offset, no record reaches into the previous segment.\n441: \t// So we can safely repair the WAL by removing the segment and re-inserting all\n442: \t// its records up to the corruption.\n443: \tw.logger.Warn(\"Rewrite corrupted segment\", \"segment\", cerr.Segment)\n444: \n445: \tfn := SegmentName(w.Dir(), cerr.Segment)\n446: \ttmpfn := fn + \".repair\"\n447: \n448: \tif err := fileutil.Rename(fn, tmpfn); err != nil {\n449: \t\treturn err\n450: \t}\n451: \t// Create a clean segment and make it the active one.\n452: \ts, err := CreateSegment(w.Dir(), cerr.Segment)\n453: \tif err != nil {\n454: \t\treturn err\n455: \t}\n456: \tif err := w.setSegment(s); err != nil {\n457: \t\treturn err\n458: \t}\n459: \n460: \tf, err := os.Open(tmpfn)\n461: \tif err != nil {\n462: \t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"open segment: %w\", err)\n463: \t}\n464: \tdefer f.Close()\n465: \n466: \tr := NewReader(bufio.NewReader(f))\n467: \n468: \tfor r.Next() {\n469: \t\t// Add records only up to the where the error was.\n470: \t\tif r.Offset() >= cerr.Offset {\n471: \t\t\tbreak\n472: \t\t}\n473: \t\tif err := w.Log(r.Record()); err != nil {\n474: \t\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"insert record: %w\", err)\n475: \t\t}\n476: \t}\n477: \t// We expect an error here from r.Err(), so nothing to handle.\n478: \n479: \t// We need to pad to the end of the last page in the repaired segment\n480: \tif err := w.flushPage(true); err != nil {\n481: \t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"flush page in repair: %w\", err)\n482: \t}\n483: \n484: \t// We explicitly close even when there is a defer for Windows to be\n485: \t// able to delete it. The defer is in place to close it in-case there\n486: \t// are errors above.\n487: \tif err := f.Close(); err != nil {\n488: \t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"close corrupted file: %w\", err)\n489: \t}\n490: \tif err := os.Remove(tmpfn); err != nil {\n491: \t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"delete corrupted segment: %w\", err)\n492: \t}\n493: \n494: \t// Explicitly close the segment we just repaired to avoid issues with Windows.\n495: \ts.Close()\n496: \n497: \t// We always want to start writing to a new Segment rather than an existing\n498: \t// Segment, which is handled by NewSize, but earlier in Repair we're deleting\n499: \t// all segments that come after the corrupted Segment. Recreate a new Segment here.\n500: \ts, err = CreateSegment(w.Dir(), cerr.Segment+1)\n501: \tif err != nil {\n502: \t\treturn err\n503: \t}\n504: \treturn w.setSegment(s)\n505: }\n506: \n507: // SegmentName builds a segment name for the directory.\n508: func SegmentName(dir string, i int) string {\n509: \treturn filepath.Join(dir, fmt.Sprintf(\"%08d\", i))\n510: }\n511: \n512: // NextSegment creates the next segment and closes the previous one asynchronously.\n513: // It returns the file number of the new file.\n514: func (w *WL) NextSegment() (int, error) {\n515: \tw.mtx.Lock()\n516: \tdefer w.mtx.Unlock()\n517: \treturn w.nextSegment(true)\n518: }\n519: \n520: // NextSegmentSync creates the next segment and closes the previous one in sync.\n521: // It returns the file number of the new file.\n522: func (w *WL) NextSegmentSync() (int, error) {\n523: \tw.mtx.Lock()\n524: \tdefer w.mtx.Unlock()\n525: \treturn w.nextSegment(false)\n526: }\n527: \n528: // nextSegment creates the next segment and closes the previous one.\n529: // It returns the file number of the new file.\n530: func (w *WL) nextSegment(async bool) (int, error) {\n531: \tif w.closed {\n532: \t\treturn 0, errors.New(\"wlog is closed\")\n533: \t}\n534: \n535: \t// Only flush the current page if it actually holds data.\n536: \tif w.page.alloc > 0 {\n537: \t\tif err := w.flushPage(true); err != nil {\n538: \t\t\treturn 0, err\n539: \t\t}\n540: \t}\n541: \tnext, err := CreateSegment(w.Dir(), w.segment.Index()+1)\n542: \tif err != nil {\n543: \t\treturn 0, fmt.Errorf(\"create new segment file: %w\", err)\n544: \t}\n545: \tprev := w.segment\n546: \tif err := w.setSegment(next); err != nil {\n547: \t\treturn 0, err\n548: \t}\n549: \n550: \t// Don't block further writes by fsyncing the last segment.\n551: \tf := func() {\n552: \t\tif err := w.fsync(prev); err != nil {\n553: \t\t\tw.logger.Error(\"sync previous segment\", \"err\", err)\n554: \t\t}\n555: \t\tif err := prev.Close(); err != nil {\n556: \t\t\tw.logger.Error(\"close previous segment\", \"err\", err)\n557: \t\t}\n558: \t}\n559: \tif async {\n560: \t\tw.actorc <- f\n561: \t} else {\n562: \t\tf()\n563: \t}\n564: \treturn next.Index(), nil\n565: }\n566: \n567: func (w *WL) setSegment(segment *Segment) error {\n568: \tw.segment = segment\n569: \n570: \t// Correctly initialize donePages.\n571: \tstat, err := segment.Stat()\n572: \tif err != nil {\n573: \t\treturn err\n574: \t}\n575: \tw.donePages = int(stat.Size() / pageSize)\n576: \tw.metrics.currentSegment.Set(float64(segment.Index()))\n577: \treturn nil\n578: }\n579: \n580: // flushPage writes the new contents of the page to disk. If no more records will fit into\n581: // the page, the remaining bytes will be set to zero and a new page will be started.\n582: // If forceClear is true, this is enforced regardless of how many bytes are left in the page.\n583: func (w *WL) flushPage(forceClear bool) error {\n584: \tw.metrics.pageFlushes.Inc()\n585: \n586: \tp := w.page\n587: \tshouldClear := forceClear || p.full()\n588: \n589: \t// No more data will fit into the page or an implicit clear.\n590: \t// Enqueue and clear it.\n591: \tif shouldClear {\n592: \t\tp.alloc = pageSize // Write till end of page.\n593: \t}\n594: \n595: \tn, err := w.segment.Write(p.buf[p.flushed:p.alloc])\n596: \tif err != nil {\n597: \t\tp.flushed += n\n598: \t\treturn err\n599: \t}\n600: \tp.flushed += n\n601: \n602: \t// We flushed an entire page, prepare a new one.\n603: \tif shouldClear {\n604: \t\tp.reset()\n605: \t\tw.donePages++\n606: \t\tw.metrics.pageCompletions.Inc()\n607: \t}\n608: \treturn nil\n609: }\n610: \n611: // First Byte of header format:\n612: //\n613: //\t[3 bits unallocated] [1 bit zstd compression flag] [1 bit snappy compression flag] [3 bit record type ]\n614: const (\n615: \tsnappyMask  = 1 << 3\n616: \tzstdMask    = 1 << 4\n617: \trecTypeMask = snappyMask - 1\n618: )\n619: \n620: type recType uint8\n621: \n622: const (\n623: \trecPageTerm recType = 0 // Rest of page is empty.\n624: \trecFull     recType = 1 // Full record.\n625: \trecFirst    recType = 2 // First fragment of a record.\n626: \trecMiddle   recType = 3 // Middle fragments of a record.\n627: \trecLast     recType = 4 // Final fragment of a record.\n628: )\n629: \n630: func recTypeFromHeader(header byte) recType {\n631: \treturn recType(header & recTypeMask)\n632: }\n633: \n634: func (t recType) String() string {\n635: \tswitch t {\n636: \tcase recPageTerm:\n637: \t\treturn \"zero\"\n638: \tcase recFull:\n639: \t\treturn \"full\"\n640: \tcase recFirst:\n641: \t\treturn \"first\"\n642: \tcase recMiddle:\n643: \t\treturn \"middle\"\n644: \tcase recLast:\n645: \t\treturn \"last\"\n646: \tdefault:\n647: \t\treturn \"<invalid>\"\n648: \t}\n649: }\n650: \n651: func (w *WL) pagesPerSegment() int {\n652: \treturn w.segmentSize / pageSize\n653: }\n654: \n655: // Log writes the records into the log.\n656: // Multiple records can be passed at once to reduce writes and increase throughput.\n657: func (w *WL) Log(recs ...[]byte) error {\n658: \tw.mtx.Lock()\n659: \tdefer w.mtx.Unlock()\n660: \t// Callers could just implement their own list record format but adding\n661: \t// a bit of extra logic here frees them from that overhead.\n662: \tfor i, r := range recs {\n663: \t\tif err := w.log(r, i == len(recs)-1); err != nil {\n664: \t\t\tw.metrics.writesFailed.Inc()\n665: \t\t\treturn err\n666: \t\t}\n667: \t}\n668: \treturn nil\n669: }\n670: \n671: // log writes rec to the log and forces a flush of the current page if:\n672: // - the final record of a batch\n673: // - the record is bigger than the page size\n674: // - the current page is full.\n675: func (w *WL) log(rec []byte, final bool) error {\n676: \t// When the last page flush failed the page will remain full.\n677: \t// When the page is full, need to flush it before trying to add more records to it.\n678: \tif w.page.full() {\n679: \t\tif err := w.flushPage(true); err != nil {\n680: \t\t\treturn err\n681: \t\t}\n682: \t}\n683: \n684: \t// Compress the record before calculating if a new segment is needed.\n685: \tfinalCompression := w.compress\n686: \tenc, err := compression.Encode(w.compress, rec, w.cEnc)\n687: \tif err != nil {\n688: \t\treturn err\n689: \t}\n690: \tif w.compress != compression.None {\n691: \t\tsavedBytes := len(rec) - len(enc)\n692: \n693: \t\t// Even if the compression was applied, skip it, if there's no benefit\n694: \t\t// in the WAL record size (we have a choice). For small records e.g. snappy\n695: \t\t// compression can yield larger records than the uncompressed.\n696: \t\tif savedBytes <= 0 {\n697: \t\t\tenc = rec\n698: \t\t\tfinalCompression = compression.None\n699: \t\t\tsavedBytes = 0\n700: \t\t}\n701: \t\tw.metrics.recordBytesSaved.WithLabelValues(w.compress).Add(float64(savedBytes))\n702: \t}\n703: \n704: \t// If the record is too big to fit within the active page in the current\n705: \t// segment, terminate the active segment and advance to the next one.\n706: \t// This ensures that records do not cross segment boundaries.\n707: \tleft := w.page.remaining() - recordHeaderSize                                   // Free space in the active page.\n708: \tleft += (pageSize - recordHeaderSize) * (w.pagesPerSegment() - w.donePages - 1) // Free pages in the active segment.\n709: \n710: \tif len(enc) > left {\n711: \t\tif _, err := w.nextSegment(true); err != nil {\n712: \t\t\treturn err\n713: \t\t}\n714: \t}\n715: \n716: \t// Populate as many pages as necessary to fit the record.\n717: \t// Be careful to always do one pass to ensure we write zero-length records.\n718: \tfor i := 0; i == 0 || len(enc) > 0; i++ {\n719: \t\tp := w.page\n720: \n721: \t\t// Find how much of the record we can fit into the page.\n722: \t\tvar (\n723: \t\t\tl    = min(len(enc), (pageSize-p.alloc)-recordHeaderSize)\n724: \t\t\tpart = enc[:l]\n725: \t\t\tbuf  = p.buf[p.alloc:]\n726: \t\t\ttyp  recType\n727: \t\t)\n728: \n729: \t\tswitch {\n730: \t\tcase i == 0 && len(part) == len(enc):\n731: \t\t\ttyp = recFull\n732: \t\tcase len(part) == len(enc):\n733: \t\t\ttyp = recLast\n734: \t\tcase i == 0:\n735: \t\t\ttyp = recFirst\n736: \t\tdefault:\n737: \t\t\ttyp = recMiddle\n738: \t\t}\n739: \n740: \t\tif finalCompression != compression.None {\n741: \t\t\tswitch finalCompression {\n742: \t\t\tcase compression.Snappy:\n743: \t\t\t\ttyp |= snappyMask\n744: \t\t\tcase compression.Zstd:\n745: \t\t\t\ttyp |= zstdMask\n746: \t\t\tdefault:\n747: \t\t\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"unsupported compression type: %v\", finalCompression)\n748: \t\t\t}\n749: \t\t}\n750: \n751: \t\tbuf[0] = byte(typ)\n752: \t\tcrc := crc32.Checksum(part, castagnoliTable)\n753: \t\tbinary.BigEndian.PutUint16(buf[1:], uint16(len(part)))\n754: \t\tbinary.BigEndian.PutUint32(buf[3:], crc)\n755: \n756: \t\tcopy(buf[recordHeaderSize:], part)\n757: \t\tp.alloc += len(part) + recordHeaderSize\n758: \n759: \t\tw.metrics.recordPartWrites.Inc()\n760: \t\tw.metrics.recordPartBytes.Add(float64(len(part) + recordHeaderSize))\n761: \n762: \t\tif w.page.full() {\n763: \t\t\tif err := w.flushPage(true); err != nil {\n764: \t\t\t\t// TODO When the flushing fails at this point and the record has not been\n765: \t\t\t\t// fully written to the buffer, we end up with a corrupted WAL because some part of the\n766: \t\t\t\t// record have been written to the buffer, while the rest of the record will be discarded.\n767: \t\t\t\treturn err\n768: \t\t\t}\n769: \t\t}\n770: \t\tenc = enc[l:]\n771: \t}\n772: \n773: \t// If it's the final record of the batch and the page is not empty, flush it.\n774: \tif final && w.page.alloc > 0 {\n775: \t\tif err := w.flushPage(false); err != nil {\n776: \t\t\treturn err\n777: \t\t}\n778: \t}\n779: \n780: \treturn nil\n781: }\n782: \n783: // LastSegmentAndOffset returns the last segment number of the WAL\n784: // and the offset in that file upto which the segment has been filled.\n785: func (w *WL) LastSegmentAndOffset() (seg, offset int, err error) {\n786: \tw.mtx.Lock()\n787: \tdefer w.mtx.Unlock()\n788: \n789: \t_, seg, err = Segments(w.Dir())\n790: \tif err != nil {\n791: \t\treturn seg, offset, err\n792: \t}\n793: \n794: \toffset = (w.donePages * pageSize) + w.page.alloc\n795: \n796: \treturn seg, offset, err\n797: }\n798: \n799: // Truncate drops all segments before i.\n800: func (w *WL) Truncate(i int) (err error) {\n801: \tw.metrics.truncateTotal.Inc()\n802: \tdefer func() {\n803: \t\tif err != nil {\n804: \t\t\tw.metrics.truncateFail.Inc()\n805: \t\t}\n806: \t}()\n807: \trefs, err := listSegments(w.Dir())\n808: \tif err != nil {\n809: \t\treturn err\n810: \t}\n811: \tfor _, r := range refs {\n812: \t\tif r.index >= i {\n813: \t\t\tbreak\n814: \t\t}\n815: \t\tif err = os.Remove(filepath.Join(w.Dir(), r.name)); This function is meant\n830: // to be used only on tests due to different behaviour on Operating Systems\n831: // like windows and linux.\n832: func (w *WL) Sync() error {\n833: \treturn w.fsync(w.segment)\n834: }\n835: \n836: // Close flushes all writes and closes active segment.\n837: func (w *WL) Close() (err error) {\n838: \tw.mtx.Lock()\n839: \tdefer w.mtx.Unlock()\n840: \n841: \tif w.closed {\n842: \t\treturn errors.New(\"wlog already closed\")\n843: \t}\n844: \n845: \tif w.segment == nil {\n846: \t\tw.closed = true\n847: \t\treturn nil\n848: \t}\n849: \n850: \t// Flush the last page and zero out all its remaining size.\n851: \t// We must not flush an empty page as it would falsely signal\n852: \t// the segment is done if we start writing to it again after opening.\n853: \tif w.page.alloc > 0 {\n854: \t\tif err := w.flushPage(true); \t\t\trecord.EncodeFloatHistogram(&buf, s.lastFloatHistogramValue)\n1202: \t\t}\n1203: \t}\n1204: \ts.Unlock()\n1205: \n1206: \treturn buf.Get()\n1207: }\n1208: \n1209: func decodeSeriesFromChunkSnapshot(d *record.Decoder, b []byte) (csr chunkSnapshotRecord, err error) {\n1210: \tdec := encoding.Decbuf{B: b}\n1211: \n1212: \tif flag := dec.Byte(); flag != \tcsr.mc.maxTime = dec.Be64int64()\n1229: \tenc := chunkenc.Encoding(dec.Byte())\n1230: \n1231: \t// The underlying bytes gets re-used later, so make a copy.\n1232: \tchunkBytes := dec.UvarintBytes()\n1233: \tchunkBytesCopy := make([]byte, len(chunkBytes))\n1234: \tcopy(chunkBytesCopy, chunkBytes)\n1235: \n1236: \tchk, err := chunkenc.FromData(enc, chunkBytesCopy)\n1237: \tif csr.lastFloatHistogramValue)\n1257: \t}\n1258: \n1259: \terr = dec.Err()\n1260: \tif err != nil && len(dec.B) > 0 {\n1261: \t\terr = fmt.Errorf(\"unexpected %d bytes left in entry\", len(dec.B))\n1262: \t}\n1263: \n1264: \treturn csr, err\n1265: }\n1266: \n1267: func encodeTombstonesToSnapshotRecord(tr tombstones.Reader) ([]byte, error) {\n1268: \tbuf := encoding.Encbuf{}\n1269: \n1270: \tbuf.PutByte(chunkSnapshotRecordTypeTombstones)\n1271: \tb, err := tombstones.Encode(tr)\n1272: \tif err != nil {\n1273: \t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"encode tombstones: %w\", err)\n1274: \t}\n1275: \tbuf.PutUvarintBytes(b)\n1276: \n1277: \treturn buf.Get(), nil\n1278: }\n1279: \n1280: func decodeTombstonesSnapshotRecord(b []byte) (tombstones.Reader, error) {\n1281: \tdec := encoding.Decbuf{B: b}\n1282: \n1283: \tif flag := dec.Byte(); flag != chunkSnapshotRecordTypeTombstones {\n1284: \t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"invalid record type %x\", flag)\n1285: \t}\n1286: \n1287: \ttr, err := tombstones.Decode(dec.UvarintBytes())\n1288: \tif err != nil {\n1289: \t\treturn tr, fmt.Errorf(\"decode tombstones: %w\", err)\n1290: \t}\n1291: \treturn tr, nil\n1292: }\n1293: \n1294: const chunkSnapshotPrefix = \"chunk_snapshot.\"\n1295: \n1296: // ChunkSnapshot creates a snapshot of all the series and tombstones in the head.\n1297: // It deletes the old chunk snapshots if the chunk snapshot creation is successful.\n1298: //\n1299: // The chunk snapshot is stored in a directory named chunk_snapshot.N.M and is written\n1300: // using the WAL package. N is the last WAL segment present during snapshotting and\n1301: // M is the offset in segment N upto which data was written.\n1302: //\n1303: // The snapshot first contains all series (each in individual records and not sorted), followed by\n1304: // tombstones (a single record), and finally exemplars (>= 1 record). Exemplars are in the order they\n1305: // were written to the circular buffer.\n1306: func (h *Head) ChunkSnapshot() (*ChunkSnapshotStats, error) {\n1307: \tif h.wal == nil {\n1308: \t\t// If we are not storing any WAL, does not make sense to take a snapshot too.\n1309: \t\th.logger.Warn(\"skipping chunk snapshotting as WAL is disabled\")\n1310: \t\treturn &ChunkSnapshotStats{}, nil\n1311: \t}\n1312: \th.chunkSnapshotMtx.Lock()\n1313: \tdefer h.chunkSnapshotMtx.Unlock()\n1314: \n1315: \tstats := &ChunkSnapshotStats{}\n1316: \n1317: \twlast, woffset, err := h.wal.LastSegmentAndOffset()\n1318: \tif err != nil && !errors.Is(err, record.ErrNotFound) {\n1319: \t\treturn stats, fmt.Errorf(\"get last wal segment and offset: %w\", err)\n1320: \t}\n1321: \n1322: \t_, cslast, csoffset, err := LastChunkSnapshot(h.opts.ChunkDirRoot)\n1323: \tif err != nil && !errors.Is(err, record.ErrNotFound) {\n1324: \t\treturn stats, fmt.Errorf(\"find last chunk snapshot: %w\", err)\n1325: \t}\n1326: \n1327: \tif wlast == cslast && woffset == csoffset {\n1328: \t\t// Nothing has been written to the WAL/Head since the last snapshot.\n1329: \t\treturn stats, nil\n1330: \t}\n1331: \n1332: \tsnapshotName := chunkSnapshotDir(wlast, woffset)\n1333: \n1334: \tcpdir := filepath.Join(h.opts.ChunkDirRoot, snapshotName)\n1335: \tcpdirtmp := cpdir + \".tmp\"\n1336: \tstats.Dir = cpdir\n1337: \n1338: \tif err := os.MkdirAll(cpdirtmp, 0o777); err != nil {\n1339: \t\treturn stats, fmt.Errorf(\"create chunk snapshot dir: %w\", err)\n1340: \t}\n1341: \tcp, err := wlog.New(nil, nil, cpdirtmp, h.wal.CompressionType())\n1342: \tif err != nil {\n1343: \t\treturn stats, fmt.Errorf(\"open chunk snapshot: %w\", err)\n1344: \t}\n1345: \n1346: \t// Ensures that an early return caused by an error doesn't leave any tmp files.\n1347: \tdefer func() {\n1348: \t\tcp.Close()\n1349: \t\tos.RemoveAll(cpdirtmp)\n1350: \t}()\n1351: \n1352: \tvar (\n1353: \t\tbuf  []byte\n1354: \t\trecs [][]byte\n1355: \t)\n1356: \t// Add all series to the snapshot.\n1357: \tstripeSize := h.series.size\n1358: \tfor i := range stripeSize {\n1359: \t\th.series.locks[i].RLock()\n1360: \n1361: \t\tfor _, s := range h.series.series[i] {\n1362: \t\t\tstart := len(buf)\n1363: \t\t\tbuf = s.encodeToSnapshotRecord(buf)\n1364: \t\t\tif len(buf[start:]) == 0 {\n1365: \t\t\t\tcontinue // All contents discarded.\n1366: \t\t\t}\n1367: \t\t\trecs = append(recs, buf[start:])\n1368: \t\t\t// Flush records in 10 MB increments.\n1369: \t\t\tif len(buf) > 10*1024*1024 {\n1370: \t\t\t\tif err := cp.Log(recs...); err != nil {\n1371: \t\t\t\t\th.series.locks[i].RUnlock()\n1372: \t\t\t\t\treturn stats, fmt.Errorf(\"flush records: %w\", err)\n1373: \t\t\t\t}\n1374: \t\t\t\tbuf, recs = buf[:0], recs[:0]\n1375: \t\t\t}\n1376: \t\t}\n1377: \t\tstats.TotalSeries += len(h.series.series[i])\n1378: \n1379: \t\th.series.locks[i].RUnlock()\n1380: \t}\n1381: \n1382: \t// Add tombstones to the snapshot.\n1383: \ttombstonesReader, err := h.Tombstones()\n1384: \tif err != nil {\n1385: \t\treturn stats, fmt.Errorf(\"get tombstones: %w\", err)\n1386: \t}\n1387: \trec, err := encodeTombstonesToSnapshotRecord(tombstonesReader)\n1388: \tif err != nil {\n1389: \t\treturn stats, fmt.Errorf(\"encode tombstones: %w\", err)\n1390: \t}\n1391: \trecs = append(recs, rec)\n1392: \t// Flush remaining series records and tombstones.\n1393: \tif err := cp.Log(recs...); err != nil {\n1394: \t\treturn stats, fmt.Errorf(\"flush records: %w\", err)\n1395: \t}\n1396: \tbuf = buf[:0]\n1397: \n1398: \t// Add exemplars in the snapshot.\n1399: \t// We log in batches, with each record having upto 10000 exemplars.\n1400: \t// Assuming 100 bytes (overestimate) per exemplar, that's ~1MB.\n1401: \tmaxExemplarsPerRecord := 10000\n1402: \tbatch := make([]record.RefExemplar, 0, maxExemplarsPerRecord)\n1403: \tenc := record.Encoder{}\n1404: \tflushExemplars := func() error {\n1405: \t\tif len(batch) == 0 {\n1406: \t\t\treturn nil\n1407: \t\t}\n1408: \t\tbuf = buf[:0]\n1409: \t\tencbuf := encoding.Encbuf{B: buf}\n1410: \t\tencbuf.PutByte(chunkSnapshotRecordTypeExemplars)\n1411: \t\tenc.EncodeExemplarsIntoBuffer(batch, &encbuf)\n1412: \t\tif err := cp.Log(encbuf.Get()); err != nil {\n1413: \t\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"log exemplars: %w\", err)\n1414: \t\t}\n1415: \t\tbuf, batch = buf[:0], batch[:0]\n1416: \t\treturn nil\n1417: \t}\n1418: \terr = h.exemplars.IterateExemplars(func(seriesLabels labels.Labels, e exemplar.Exemplar) error {\n1419: \t\tif len(batch) >= maxExemplarsPerRecord {\n1420: \t\t\tif err := flushExemplars(); err != nil {\n1421: \t\t\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"flush exemplars: %w\", err)\n1422: \t\t\t}\n1423: \t\t}\n1424: \n1425: \t\tms := h.series.getByHash(seriesLabels.Hash(), seriesLabels)\n1426: \t\tif ms == nil {\n1427: \t\t\t// It is possible that exemplar refers to some old series. We discard such exemplars.\n1428: \t\t\treturn nil\n1429: \t\t}\n1430: \t\tbatch = append(batch, record.RefExemplar{\n1431: \t\t\tRef:    ms.ref,\n1432: \t\t\tT:      e.Ts,\n1433: \t\t\tV:      e.Value,\n1434: \t\t\tLabels: e.Labels,\n1435: \t\t})\n1436: \t\treturn nil\n1437: \t})\n1438: \tif err != nil {\n1439: \t\treturn stats, fmt.Errorf(\"iterate exemplars: %w\", err)\n1440: \t}\n1441: \n1442: \t// Flush remaining exemplars.\n1443: \tif err := flushExemplars(); err != nil {\n1444: \t\treturn stats, fmt.Errorf(\"flush exemplars at the end: %w\", err)\n1445: \t}\n1446: \n1447: \tif err := cp.Close(); err != nil {\n1448: \t\treturn stats, fmt.Errorf(\"close chunk snapshot: %w\", err)\n1449: \t}\n1450: \tif err := fileutil.Replace(cpdirtmp, cpdir); err != nil {\n1451: \t\treturn stats, fmt.Errorf(\"rename chunk snapshot directory: %w\", err)\n1452: \t}\n1453: \n1454: \tif err := DeleteChunkSnapshots(h.opts.ChunkDirRoot, wlast, woffset); err != nil {\n1455: \t\t// Leftover old chunk snapshots do not cause problems down the line beyond\n1456: \t\t// occupying disk space.\n1457: \t\t// They will just be ignored since a higher chunk snapshot exists.\n1458: \t\th.logger.Error(\"delete old chunk snapshots\", \"err\", err)\n1459: \t}\n1460: \treturn stats, nil\n1461: }\n1462: \n1463: func chunkSnapshotDir(wlast, woffset int) string {\n1464: \treturn fmt.Sprintf(chunkSnapshotPrefix+\"%06d.%010d\", wlast, woffset)\n1465: }\n1466: \n1467: func (h *Head) performChunkSnapshot() error {\n1468: \th.logger.Info(\"creating chunk snapshot\")\n1469: \tstartTime := time.Now()\n1470: \tstats, err := h.ChunkSnapshot()\n1471: \telapsed := time.Since(startTime)\n1472: \tif err != nil {\n1473: \t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"chunk snapshot: %w\", err)\n1474: \t}\n1475: \th.logger.Info(\"chunk snapshot complete\", \"duration\", elapsed.String(), \"num_series\", stats.TotalSeries, \"dir\", stats.Dir)\n1476: \treturn nil\n1477: }\n1478: \n1479: // ChunkSnapshotStats returns stats about a created chunk snapshot.\n1480: type ChunkSnapshotStats struct {\n1481: \tTotalSeries int\n1482: \tDir         string\n1483: }\n1484: \n1485: // LastChunkSnapshot returns the directory name and index of the most recent chunk snapshot.\n1486: // If dir does not contain any chunk snapshots, ErrNotFound is returned.\n1487: func LastChunkSnapshot(dir string) (string, int, int, error) {\n1488: \tfiles, err := os.ReadDir(dir)\n1489: \tif err != nil {\n1490: \t\treturn \"\", 0, 0, err\n1491: \t}\n1492: \tmaxIdx, maxOffset := -1, \n8: ## Segment filename\n9: \n10: The sequence number is captured in the segment filename,\n11: e.g. `000000`, `000001`, `000002`, etc. The first unsigned integer represents\n12: the sequence number of the segment, typically encoded with six digits.\n13: \n14: ## Segment encoding\n15: \n16: This section describes the segment encoding.\n17: \n18: A segment encodes an array of records. It does not contain any header. A segment\n19: is written to pages of 32KB. Only the last page of the most recent segment\n20: may be partial. A WAL record is an opaque byte slice that gets split up into sub-records\n21: should it exceed the remaining space of the current page. Records are never split across\n22: segment boundaries. provides the `WL` struct that manages the write-ahead log lifecycle. Key functions include:\\n- `CreateSegment()` and `OpenWriteSegment()` for segment creation and opening\\n- `NextSegment()` and `NextSegmentSync()` for segment rotation when the current segment reaches size limits (default 128MB)\\n- `Log()` for writing records to the WAL with automatic page flushing (32KB pages) and segment rotation\\n- `Truncate()` for removing old segments after checkpointing\\n- `Segments()` for querying available segment ranges\\nThe WL manages page-based buffering to batch disk writes and ensures records never cross segment boundaries.\\n\\n## Record Encoding/Decoding (tsdb/record/record.go)\\nThe `tsdb/record/record.go` package implements the record encoding format with two main components:\\n- `Encoder` struct that serializes various record types: Series (RefSeries with labels), Samples (RefSample with timestamp/value), Tombstones (deletion markers), Exemplars (RefExemplar), Metadata (RefMetadata with unit/help), and Histogram samples (RefHistogramSample and RefFloatHistogramSample) with custom buckets support\\n- `Decoder` struct that deserializes these record types, handling label encoding/decoding, delta compression for timestamps and series references, and histogram schema validation\\nThe encoding supports compression (Snappy/Zstd) to reduce WAL file size.\\n\\n## WAL Reader Implementations\\nTwo reader implementations handle WAL consumption:\\n- `tsdb/wlog/reader.go` provides the `Reader` struct for reading completed WAL segments with CRC32 checksum validation and record type validation (detecting torn records)\\n- `tsdb/wlog/live_reader.go` provides the `LiveReader` struct for reading WAL segments that are still being written, enabling concurrent WAL processing\\n\\n## Checkpoint Creation (tsdb/wlog/checkpoint.go)\\nThe checkpoint system creates compacted snapshots of WAL segments to enable WAL truncation:\\n- `Checkpoint()` function processes WAL segments [from, to], reads records through Decoder, filters old data (based on mint timestamp and keep function), and writes compacted records through Encoder\\n- `LastCheckpoint()` finds the most recent checkpoint directory\\n- `DeleteCheckpoints()` removes old checkpoint directories after WAL truncation\\n- `DeleteTempCheckpoints()` cleans up failed checkpoint attempts\\nCheckpoints are stored in `checkpoint.XXXXXXXX` directories using the same segmented WAL format, enabling easy concatenation with remaining WAL segments.\\n\\n## WAL Corruption Repair (tsdb/wlog/wlog.go)\\nThe `Repair()` function handles corruption detection and recovery:\\n- Accepts `CorruptionErr` with segment index and offset information\\n- Deletes all segments after the corrupted segment\\n- Rewrites the corrupted segment by reading valid records up to the corruption point\\n- Creates a new segment for continued writing\\nThis strategy preserves as much data as possible while ensuring consistency.\\n\\n## WAL Watching (tsdb/wlog/watcher.go)\\nThe `Watcher` struct monitors the WAL for changes in real-time:\\n- Implements periodic WAL segment checking and processing\\n- Calls `WriteTo` interface methods to dispatch Series, Samples, Exemplars, Histograms, and Metadata records\\n- Tracks segment indices for series garbage collection\\n- Supports metadata and histogram sample handling\\n\\n## Integration Points\\nThe WAL is integrated with the TSDB head block (tsdb/head_wal.go) which:\\n- Replays WAL records on startup to restore in-memory data\\n- Logs series, samples, and metadata changes during normal operation\\n- Triggers checkpointing based on WAL segment count\\n- Calls `Repair()` on detected corruption errors\\n\\nAll WAL operations are designed to be crash-safe using page-based writes, CRC checksums, and segment management, record encoding/decoding, corruption repair, and checkpoint creation.\\n\\n## Core WAL Segment Management (tsdb/wlog/wlog.go)\\nThe primary WAL implementation in `tsdb/wlog/wlog.go` provides the `WL` struct that manages the write-ahead log lifecycle. Key functions include:\\n- `CreateSegment()` and `OpenWriteSegment()` for segment creation and opening\\n- `NextSegment()` and `NextSegmentSync()` for segment rotation when the current segment reaches size limits (default 128MB)\\n- `Log()` for writing records to the WAL with automatic page flushing (32KB pages) and segment rotation\\n- `Truncate()` for removing old segments after checkpointing\\n- `Segments()` for querying available segment ranges\\nThe WL manages page-based buffering to batch disk writes and ensures records never cross segment boundaries.\\n\\n## Record Encoding/Decoding (tsdb/record/record.go)\\nThe `tsdb/record/record.go` package implements the record encoding format with two main components:\\n- `Encoder` struct that serializes various record types: Series (RefSeries with labels), Samples (RefSample with timestamp/value), Tombstones (deletion markers), Exemplars (RefExemplar), Metadata (RefMetadata with unit/help), and Histogram samples (RefHistogramSample and RefFloatHistogramSample) with custom buckets support\\n- `Decoder` struct that deserializes these record types, handling label encoding/decoding, delta compression for timestamps and series references, and histogram schema validation\\nThe encoding supports compression (Snappy/Zstd) to reduce WAL file size.\\n\\n## WAL Reader Implementations\\nTwo reader implementations handle WAL consumption:\\n- `tsdb/wlog/reader.go` provides the `Reader` struct for reading completed WAL segments with CRC32 checksum validation and record type validation (detecting torn records)\\n- `tsdb/wlog/live_reader.go` provides the `LiveReader` struct for reading WAL segments that are still being written, enabling concurrent WAL processing\\n\\n## Checkpoint Creation (tsdb/wlog/checkpoint.go)\\nThe checkpoint system creates compacted snapshots of WAL segments to enable WAL truncation:\\n- `Checkpoint()` function processes WAL segments [from, to], reads records through Decoder, filters old data (based on mint timestamp and keep function), and writes compacted records through Encoder\\n- `LastCheckpoint()` finds the most recent checkpoint directory\\n- `DeleteCheckpoints()` removes old checkpoint directories after WAL truncation\\n- `DeleteTempCheckpoints()` cleans up failed checkpoint attempts\\nCheckpoints are stored in `checkpoint.XXXXXXXX` directories using the same segmented WAL format, enabling easy concatenation with remaining WAL segments.\\n\\n## WAL Corruption Repair (tsdb/wlog/wlog.go)\\nThe `Repair()` function handles corruption detection and recovery:\\n- Accepts `CorruptionErr` with segment index and offset information\\n- Deletes all segments after the corrupted segment\\n- Rewrites the corrupted segment by reading valid records up to the corruption point\\n- Creates a new segment for continued writing\\nThis strategy preserves as much data as possible while ensuring consistency.\\n\\n## WAL Watching (tsdb/wlog/watcher.go)\\nThe `Watcher` struct monitors the WAL for changes in real-time:\\n- Implements periodic WAL segment checking and processing\\n- Calls `WriteTo` interface methods to dispatch Series, Samples, Exemplars, Histograms, and Metadata records\\n- Tracks segment indices for series garbage collection\\n- Supports metadata and histogram sample handling\\n\\n## Integration Points\\nThe WAL is integrated with the TSDB head block (tsdb/head_wal.go) which:\\n- Replays WAL records on startup to restore in-memory data\\n- Logs series, samples, and metadata changes during normal operation\\n- Triggers checkpointing based on WAL segment count\\n- Calls `Repair()` on detected corruption errors\\n\\nAll WAL operations are designed to be crash-safe using page-based writes, CRC checksums, and segment atomicity.\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}

Key functions include:\\n- `CreateSegment()` and `OpenWriteSegment()` for segment creation and opening\\n- `NextSegment()` and `NextSegmentSync()` for segment rotation when the current segment reaches (RefSeries with labels), Samples (RefSample with timestamp/value), Tombstones (deletion markers), Exemplars (RefExemplar), Metadata (RefMetadata with unit/help), and Histogram samples \"tsdb/record/record.go\", \"symbol\": \"Encoder\"}\n  ],\n  \"text\": \"The Prometheus TSDB write-ahead log (WAL) implementation consists of multiple coordinated Go packages that handle segment management, record encoding/decoding, corruption repair, and checkpoint creation.\\n\\n## Core WAL Segment Management (tsdb/wlog/wlog.go)\\nThe primary WAL implementation in `tsdb/wlog/wlog.go` provides the `WL` struct that manages the write-ahead log lifecycle. Key functions include:\\n- `CreateSegment()` and `OpenWriteSegment()` for segment creation and opening\\n- `NextSegment()` and `NextSegmentSync()` for segment rotation when the current segment reaches size limits (default 128MB)\\n- `Log()` for writing records to the WAL with automatic page flushing (32KB pages) and segment rotation\\n- `Truncate()` for removing old segments after checkpointing\\n- `Segments()` for querying available segment ranges\\nThe WL manages page-based buffering to batch disk writes and ensures records never cross segment boundaries.\\n\\n## Record Encoding/Decoding (tsdb/record/record.go)\\nThe `tsdb/record/record.go` package implements the record encoding format with two main components:\\n- `Encoder` struct that serializes various record types: Series (RefSeries with labels), Samples (RefSample with timestamp/value), Tombstones (deletion markers), Exemplars (RefExemplar), Metadata (RefMetadata with unit/help), and Histogram samples (RefHistogramSample and RefFloatHistogramSample) with custom buckets support\\n- `Decoder` struct that deserializes these record types, handling label encoding/decoding, delta compression for timestamps and series references, and histogram schema validation\\nThe encoding supports compression (Snappy/Zstd) to reduce WAL file size.\\n\\n## WAL Reader Implementations\\nTwo reader implementations handle WAL consumption:\\n- `tsdb/wlog/reader.go` provides the `Reader` struct for reading completed WAL segments with CRC32 checksum validation and record type validation (detecting torn records)\\n- `tsdb/wlog/live_reader.go` provides the `LiveReader` struct for reading WAL segments that are still being written, enabling concurrent WAL processing\\n\\n## Checkpoint Creation (tsdb/wlog/checkpoint.go)\\nThe checkpoint system creates compacted snapshots of WAL segments to enable WAL truncation:\\n- `Checkpoint()` function processes WAL segments [from, to], reads records through Decoder, filters old data (based on mint timestamp and keep function), and writes compacted records through Encoder\\n- `LastCheckpoint()` finds the most recent checkpoint directory\\n- `DeleteCheckpoints()` removes old checkpoint directories after WAL truncation\\n- `DeleteTempCheckpoints()` cleans up failed checkpoint attempts\\nCheckpoints are stored in `checkpoint.XXXXXXXX` directories using the same segmented WAL format, enabling easy concatenation with remaining WAL segments.\\n\\n## WAL Corruption Repair (tsdb/wlog/wlog.go)\\nThe `Repair()` function handles corruption detection and recovery:\\n- Accepts `CorruptionErr` with segment index and offset information\\n- Deletes all segments after the corrupted segment\\n- Rewrites the corrupted segment by reading valid records up to the corruption point\\n- Creates a new segment for continued writing\\nThis strategy preserves as much data as possible while ensuring consistency.\\n\\n## WAL Watching (tsdb/wlog/watcher.go)\\nThe `Watcher` struct monitors the WAL for changes in real-time:\\n- Implements periodic WAL segment checking and processing\\n- Calls `WriteTo` interface methods to dispatch Series, Samples, Exemplars, Histograms, and Metadata records\\n- Tracks segment indices for series garbage collection\\n- Supports metadata and histogram sample handling\\n\\n## Integration Points\\nThe WAL is integrated with the TSDB head block (tsdb/head_wal.go) which:\\n- Replays WAL records on startup to restore in-memory data\\n- Logs series, samples, and metadata changes during normal operation\\n- Triggers checkpointing based on WAL segment count\\n- Calls `Repair()` on detected corruption errors\\n\\nAll WAL operations are designed to be crash-safe using page-based writes, CRC checksums, and segment atomicity.\"\n}\n","numLines":73,"startLine":1,"totalLines":73}}}
